This is a great tutorial but crayola crayons are far from natural. Their main ingredients are paraffin wax and colour pigment. Paraffin is generally not safe (and it is often mixed with other harsh chemicals when used commercially) and crayola refuse to disclose the composition of the colour pigment. Corporate companies refusing to reveal the ingredients they use = something unsafe that they'd rather not let people know about, especially since crayola is aimed at children and claim that it's 100% safe.  They do state on their website that they use ingredients which have not been proven to cause side effects in low doses. Translation: they use a little bit of toxic chemicals in each crayon. Add that up over time by using a lipstick with those chemicals (lipstick is reapplied daily so it adds up quite a lot) and you'll end up ingesting those ingredients in high doses.

So..how safe is this? Crayola doesn't even list their ingredients on the webpage. It says I can have my doctor contact the poison control center for assistance in getting the ingredients. Um..POISON control? Why..if it's non-toxic? It contains paraffin wax..which has toulene and benzene...which are toxic and known carcinogens. It's small quantities..but if you're constantly wearing the lipstick, eating, rubbing your lips, licking..you're ingesting it and over time, consuming more than is safe. I just don't know if it's worth the risk. Even most lipsticks have chemicals known to cause cancer..and the natural ones still have things like carmine for coloring, which is crushed beetles. I have a known cockroach allergy..so I still have to be careful with "natural" products because I react to carmine with a rash. It's also in gummy bears, Dannon's yogurt and many other foods.

If you live somewhere hot(or just in the summer) you might want something more stable than coconut oil. More stable options would be Shea butter, coco butter, bee wax, palm wax, soy wax. Pretty much anything that melts in heat, but will solidify back when out of the heat. I usually stick to pinksofoxy's lip balm recipe for many things.Â  She lives in Hawaii so she makes things that wont melt easily.Â  She pretty much does a mixture of bee wax, coco butter, Shea butter, even coconut oil all in moderation. I learned to be suspicious when people say to just use coconut oil in products and nothing more stable, all because I watched a video where someone just used coconut oil and a few powders to make deodorant. When I made it, the temperature was in the 90's so it was a fail.Â  I see a lot of people in the comments asking if the can use carrier oils(sunflower, olive, grape seed, almond etc) Ehhh...if you want something solid and live somewhere hot, and or want to actually put your lipstick in a classic tube container, I wouldn't risk wasting your stuff.

I think your video was very informative. However, my 7yr old son watched it yesterday, with me and He decided to get up and try it, while we were sleeping. He painted his whole body green! Thankfully he used the microwave and forgot the coconut oil step. But I thought other readers may want to know how to get the crayon off if this scenario happens to them. This is what the Crayola website says: How can I remove Crayola washable product stains from skin?  Although CRAYOLA washable products are water-based and designed to wash from skin and nearly all children's clothing, the dyes and pigments included in Crayola washable products react differently to various skin types, depending on a person's body chemistry.  Normally, Crayola washable products can be removed from the skin by washing with soap and water. If you are unsuccessful with soap and water, try using baby wipes, baby oil or make-up remover. Since Crayola washable products are water-based, you may find that keeping the area moist with water will help to lift the stain.  If you need further assistance, please call (800) 272-9652 weekdays between 9 AM and 4 PM Eastern Time and a representative will be happy to assist you.

This worked so well, but I had to make a few adjustments according to supplies I had. Here is the recipe. Ingredients: Crayola Crayon: Color of Choice Canola or Vegetable Oil Other Supplies: Small container  Directions: 1. Pour a small drop of oil into a glass bowl 2.Add an inch of a crayon into the bowl 3. Microwave the mix for a minute and a half 4. Pour the mix into the container 5. Let dry for five minutes  *NOTE: Moisturizes lips and non-toxic

Countless studies have been done on this.. even and especially artificial food dyes!! And although they are on the market still.. they shouldn't be! Here are some of the things artificial dyes can link to : â€œStudies have linked artificial dyes to behavioral problems such as ADD/ADHD and hyperactivity, as well as allergic reactions, brain cancer, tumor growth, cell deterioration, nerve and organ damage, birth defects, and uncontrolled cell mutation,â€ says Dr. Lipman. â€œCBS News reported that certain children diagnosed with ADHD may not need medication if artificial dyes were removed from their diets!â€ ^That was taken from http://www.refinery29.com/2013/08/51056/food-dye-brain-cells this site just for an example but you guys should google artificial food dye hazards etc.. Non-toxic does NOT equal safe for skin as a cosmetic. Please educate yourself before poisoning the public. "â€¢ An art material is â€œnontoxicâ€ if a toxicologist paid by the manufacturer decides it is safe. The dramatic failure in this labeling procedure was illustrated with the lead ceramic glazes and asbestos-containing materials such as talc.
